margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">PHP (\xe2\x82\xb1)</div></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">0.3%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">31</div></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></span> <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_dirham" title="United Arab Emirates dirham">UAE dirham</a></td>\n<td><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">AED (\xd8\xaf.\xd8\xa5)</div></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">0.2%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">32</div></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></span> <a href="/wiki/Colombian_peso" title="Colombian peso">Colombian peso</a></td>\n<td><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">COP (COL$)</div></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">0.2%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">33</div></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></span> <a href="/wiki/Saudi_riyal" title="Saudi riyal">Saudi riyal</a></td>\n<td><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">SAR (\xef\xb7\xbc)</div></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">0.2%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">34</div></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></span> <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_ringgit" title="Malaysian ringgit">Malaysian ringgit</a></td>\n<td><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">MYR (RM)</div></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">0.1%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">35</div></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Romania.svg/23px-Flag_of_Romania.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Romania.svg/35px-Flag_of_Romania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Romania.svg/45px-Flag_of_Romania.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></span> <a href="/wiki/Romanian_leu" title="Romanian leu">Romanian leu</a></td>\n<td><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">RON (L)</div></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">0.1%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" style="text-align:right;">Other</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.2%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" style="text-align:right;">Total<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;note 9&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">200.0%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The most obvious benefit of adopting a single currency is to remove the cost of exchanging currency, theoretically allowing businesses and individuals to consummate previously unprofitable trades. For consumers, banks in the eurozone must charge the same for intra-member cross-border transactions as purely domestic transactions for electronic payments (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Credit_card" title="Credit card">credit cards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Debit_card" title="Debit card">debit cards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cash_machine" class="mw-redirect" title="Cash machine">cash machine</a> withdrawals).\n</p><p>Financial markets on the continent are expected to be far more <a href="/wiki/Market_liquidity" title="Market liquidity">liquid</a> and flexible than they were in the past. The reduction in cross-border transaction costs will allow larger banking firms to provide a wider array of banking services that can compete across and beyond the eurozone. However, although transaction costs were reduced, some studies have shown that <a href="/wiki/Risk_aversion" title="Risk aversion">risk aversion</a> has increased during the last 40 years in the Eurozone.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Price_parity">Price parity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Price parity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Another effect of the common European currency is that differences in prices\xe2\x80\x94in particular in price levels\xe2\x80\x94should decrease because of the <a href="/wiki/Law_of_one_price" title="Law of one price">law of one price</a>. Differences in prices can trigger <a href="/wiki/Arbitrage" title="Arbitrage">arbitrage</a>, i.e., <a href="/wiki/Speculation" title="Speculation">speculative</a> trade in a <a href="/wiki/Commodity" title="Commodity">commodity</a> across borders purely to exploit the price differential. Therefore, prices on commonly traded goods are likely to converge, causing inflation in some regions and deflation in others during the transition. Some evidence of this has been observed in specific eurozone markets.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Macroeconomic_stability">Macroeconomic stability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Macroeconomic stability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Before the introduction of the euro, some countries had successfully contained inflation, which was then seen as a major economic problem, by establishing largely independent central banks. One such bank was the <a href="/wiki/Bundesbank" class="mw-redirect" title="Bundesbank">Bundesbank</a> in Germany; the European Central Bank was modelled on the Bundesbank.<sup id="cite_ref-bundesbank_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bundesbank-82">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The euro has come under criticism due to its regulation, lack of flexibility and rigidity towards sharing member States on issues such as nominal interest rates.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\nMany national and corporate <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">bonds</a> denominated in euro are significantly more liquid and have lower interest rates than was historically the case when denominated in national currencies. While increased liquidity may lower the <a href="/wiki/Nominal_interest_rate" title="Nominal interest rate">nominal interest rate</a> on the bond, denominating the bond in a currency with low levels of inflation arguably plays a much larger role. A credible commitment to low levels of inflation and a stable debt reduces the risk that the value of the debt will be eroded by higher levels of inflation or default in the future, allowing debt to be issued at a lower nominal interest rate.\n</p><p>Unfortunately, there is also a cost in structurally keeping inflation lower than in the United States, UK, and China. The result is that seen from those countries, the euro has become expensive, making European products increasingly expensive for its largest importers; hence export from the eurozone becomes more difficult.\n</p><p>In general, those in Europe who own large amounts of euros are served by high stability and low inflation.\n</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Monetary_union" class="mw-redirect" title="Monetary union">monetary union</a> means states in that union lose the main mechanism of recovery of their international <a href="/wiki/Competition_(companies)" class="mw-redirect" title="Competition (companies)">competitiveness</a> by weakening (<a href="/wiki/Currency_appreciation_and_depreciation" title="Currency appreciation and depreciation">depreciating</a>) their currency. When <a href="/wiki/Wage" title="Wage">wages</a> become too high compared to <a href="/wiki/Productivity" title="Productivity">productivity</a> in exports sector then these exports become more expensive and they are crowded out from the market within a country and abroad. This drive fall of employment and output in the exports sector and fall of <a href="/wiki/Balance_of_trade" title="Balance of trade">trade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Current_account_(balance_of_payments)" title="Current account (balance of payments)">current account</a> balances. Fall of output and employment in tradable goods sector may be offset by the growth of non-exports sectors, especially in <a href="/wiki/Construction" title="Construction">construction</a> and <a href="/wiki/Service_(economics)" title="Service (economics)">services</a>. Increased purchases abroad and negative current account balance can be financed without a problem as long as <a href="/wiki/Credit" title="Credit">credit</a> is cheap.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The need to finance trade deficit weakens currency making exports automatically more attractive in a country and abroad. A state in a monetary union cannot use weakening of currency to recover its international competitiveness. To achieve this a state has to reduce prices, including wages (<a href="/wiki/Deflation" title="Deflation">deflation</a>). This could result in high <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a> and lower incomes as it was during <a href="/wiki/European_sovereign-debt_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="European sovereign-debt crisis">European sovereign-debt crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Trade">Trade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Trade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>A 2009 consensus from the studies of the introduction of the euro concluded that it has increased trade within the eurozone by 5% to 10%,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> although one study suggested an increase of only 3%<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> while another estimated 9 to 14%.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> However, a <a href="/wiki/Meta-analysis" title="Meta-analysis">meta-analysis</a> of all available studies suggests that the prevalence of positive estimates is caused by <a href="/wiki/Publication_bias" title="Publication bias">publication bias</a> and that the underlying effect may be negligible.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Although a more recent meta-analysis shows that publication bias decreases over time and that there are positive trade effects from the introduction of the euro, as long as results from before 2010 are taken into account. This may be because of the inclusion of the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x932008">Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x932008</a> and ongoing integration within the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, older studies accounting for <a href="/wiki/Time_trend_analysis" class="mw-redirect" title="Time trend analysis">time trend</a> reflecting general cohesion policies in Europe that started before, and continue after implementing the common currency find no effect on trade.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> These results suggest that other policies aimed at European integration might be the source of observed increase in trade.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Investment">Investment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Investment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Physical investment seems to have increased by 5% in the eurozone due to the introduction.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Regarding foreign direct investment, a study found that the intra-eurozone FDI stocks have increased by about 20% during the first four years of the EMU.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Concerning the effect on corporate investment, there is evidence that the introduction of the euro has resulted in an increase in investment rates and that it has made it easier for firms to access financing in Europe. The euro has most specifically stimulated investment in companies that come from countries that previously had weak currencies. A study found that the introduction of the euro accounts for 22% of the investment rate after 1998 in countries that previously had a weak currency.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Inflation">Inflation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Inflation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The introduction of the euro has led to extensive discussion about its possible effect on inflation. In the short term, there was a widespread impression in the population of the eurozone that the introduction of the euro had led to an increase in prices, but this impression was not confirmed by general indices of inflation and other studies.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> A study of this paradox found that this was due to an asymmetric effect of the introduction of the euro on prices: while it had no effect on most goods, it had an effect on cheap goods which have seen their price round up after the introduction of the euro. The study found that consumers based their beliefs on inflation of those cheap goods which are frequently purchased.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> It has also been suggested that the jump in small prices may be because prior to the introduction, retailers made fewer upward adjustments and waited for the introduction of the euro to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Exchange_rate_risk">Exchange rate risk</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Exchange rate risk">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>One of the advantages of the adoption of a common currency is the reduction of the risk associated with changes in currency exchange rates. It has been found that the introduction of the euro created "significant reductions in market risk exposures for nonfinancial firms both in and outside Europe".<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> These reductions in market risk "were concentrated in firms domiciled in the eurozone and in non-euro firms with a high fraction of foreign sales or assets in Europe".\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_integration">Financial integration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Financial integration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The introduction of the euro seems to have had a strong effect on European financial integration. According to a study on this question, it has "significantly reshaped the European financial system, especially with respect to the securities markets [...] However, the real and policy barriers to integration in the retail and corporate banking sectors remain significant, even if the wholesale end of banking has been largely integrated."<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Specifically, the euro has significantly decreased the cost of trade in bonds, equity, and banking assets within the eurozone.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> On a global level, there is evidence that the introduction of the euro has led to an integration in terms of investment in bond portfolios, with eurozone countries lending and borrowing more between each other than with other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Effect_on_interest_rates">Effect on interest rates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Effect on interest rates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Long-term_interest_rates_of_eurozone_countries_since_1993.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Long-term_interest_rates_of_eurozone_countries_since_1993.png/300px-Long-term_interest_rates_of_eurozone_countries_since_1993.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Long-term_interest_rates_of_eurozone_countries_since_1993.png/450px-Long-term_interest_rates_of_eurozone_countries_since_1993.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Long-term_interest_rates_of_eurozone_countries_since_1993.png/600px-Long-term_interest_rates_of_eurozone_countries_since_1993.png 2x" data-file-width="1337" data-file-height="638" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Long-term_interest_rates_of_eurozone_countries_since_1993.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Secondary market yields of government bonds with maturities of close to 10 years</div></div></div>\n<p>As of January 2014, and since the introduction of the euro, interest rates of most member countries (particularly those with a weak currency) have decreased. Some of these countries had the most serious sovereign financing problems.\n</p><p>The effect of declining interest rates, combined with excess liquidity continually provided by the ECB, made it easier for banks within the countries in which interest rates fell the most, and their linked sovereigns, to borrow significant amounts (above the 3% of GDP budget deficit imposed on the eurozone initially) and significantly inflate their public and private debt levels.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x932008">financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x932008</a>, governments in these countries found it necessary to bail out or nationalise their privately held banks to prevent systemic failure of the banking system when underlying hard or financial asset values were found to be grossly inflated and sometimes so near worthless there was no liquid market for them.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> This further increased the already high levels of public debt to a level the markets began to consider unsustainable, via increasing government bond interest rates, producing the ongoing European sovereign-debt crisis.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Price_convergence">Price convergence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Price convergence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The evidence on the convergence of prices in the eurozone with the introduction of the euro is mixed. Several studies failed to find any evidence of convergence following the introduction of the euro after a phase of convergence in the early 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Other studies have found evidence of price convergence,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> in particular for cars.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> A possible reason for the divergence between the different studies is that the processes of convergence may not have been linear, slowing down substantially between 2000 and 2003, and resurfacing after 2003 as suggested by a recent study (2009).<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>A study suggests that the introduction of the euro has had a positive effect on the amount of tourist travel within the EMU, with an increase of 6.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Exchange_rates">Exchange rates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Exchange rates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flexible_exchange_rates">Flexible exchange rates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Flexible exchange rates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The ECB targets <a href="/wiki/Interest_rate" title="Interest rate">interest rates</a> rather than <a href="/wiki/Exchange_rate" title="Exchange rate">exchange rates</a> and in general, does not intervene on the foreign exchange rate markets. This is because of the implications of the <a href="/wiki/Mundell%E2%80%93Fleming_model" title="Mundell\xe2\x80\x93Fleming model">Mundell\xe2\x80\x93Fleming model</a>, which implies a central bank cannot (without <a href="/wiki/Capital_control" title="Capital control">capital controls</a>) maintain interest rate and exchange rate targets simultaneously, because increasing the <a href="/wiki/Money_supply" title="Money supply">money supply</a> results in a <a href="/wiki/Depreciation" title="Depreciation">depreciation</a> of the currency. In the years following the <a href="/wiki/Single_European_Act" title="Single European Act">Single European Act</a>, the EU has liberalised its capital markets and, as the ECB has <a href="/wiki/Inflation_targeting" title="Inflation targeting">inflation targeting</a> as its <a href="/wiki/Monetary_policy" title="Monetary policy">monetary policy</a>, the exchange-rate regime of the euro is <a href="/wiki/Floating_exchange_rate" title="Floating exchange rate">floating</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Against_other_major_currencies">Against other major currencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Against other major currencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The euro is the second-most widely held <a href="/wiki/Reserve_currency" title="Reserve currency">reserve currency</a> after the U.S. dollar. After its introduction on 4 January 1999 its exchange rate against the other major currencies fell reaching its lowest exchange rates in 2000 (3 May vs <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">Pound sterling</a>, 25 October vs the <a href="/wiki/U.S._dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. dollar">U.S. dollar</a>, 26 October vs <a href="/wiki/Japanese_yen" title="Japanese yen">Japanese yen</a>). Afterwards it regained and its exchange rate reached its historical highest point in 2008 (15 July vs U.S. dollar, 23 July vs Japanese yen, 29 December vs Pound sterling). With the advent of the global financial crisis the euro initially fell, to regain later. Despite pressure due to the <a href="/wiki/European_sovereign-debt_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="European sovereign-debt crisis">European sovereign-debt crisis</a> the euro remained stable.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> In November 2011 the euro\'s exchange rate index&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 measured against currencies of the bloc\'s major trading partners&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 was trading almost two percent higher on the year, approximately at the same level as it was before the crisis kicked off in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Political considerations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Besides the economic motivations to the introduction of the euro, its creation was also partly justified as a way to foster a closer sense of joint identity between European citizens. Statements about this goal were for instance made by <a href="/wiki/Wim_Duisenberg" title="Wim Duisenberg">Wim Duisenberg</a>, European Central Bank Governor, in 1998,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Laurent_Fabius" title="Laurent Fabius">Laurent Fabius</a>, French Finance Minister, in 2000,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Romano_Prodi" title="Romano Prodi">Romano Prodi</a>, President of the European Commission, in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> However, 15 years after the introduction of the euro, a study found no evidence that it has had a positive influence on a shared sense of European identity (and no evidence that it had a negative effect either).<sup id="cite_ref-EER_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EER-118">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Linguistic_issues">Linguistic issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Linguistic issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Linguistic_issues_concerning_the_euro" class="mw-redirect" title="Linguistic issues concerning the euro">Linguistic issues concerning the euro</a></div>\n<p>The formal titles of the currency are <i>euro</i> for the major unit and <i>cent</i> for the minor (one-hundredth) unit and for official use in most eurozone languages; according to the ECB, all languages should use the same spelling for the nominative singular.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> This may contradict normal rules for word formation in some languages, e.g., those in which there is no <i>eu</i> <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthong</a>. Bulgaria has negotiated an exception; <i>euro</i> in the Bulgarian Cyrillic alphabet is spelled as e\xd0\xb2\xd1\x80\xd0\xbe (<i>evro</i>) and not e\xd1\x83\xd1\x80\xd0\xbe (<i>euro</i>) in all official documents.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In the Greek script the term \xce\xb5\xcf\x85\xcf\x81\xcf\x8e (evr\xc3\xb3) is used; the Greek "cent" coins are denominated in \xce\xbb\xce\xb5\xcf\x80\xcf\x84\xcf\x8c/\xce\xac (lept\xc3\xb3/\xc3\xa1). Official practice for English-language EU legislation is to use the words euro and cent as both singular and plural,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> although the European Commission\'s <a href="/wiki/Directorate-General_for_Translation_(European_Commission)" class="mw-redirect" title="Directorate-General for Translation (European Commission)">Directorate-General for Translation</a> states that the plural forms <i>euros</i> and <i>cents</i> should be used in English.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Except <a href="/wiki/Northern_Cyprus" title="Northern Cyprus">Northern Cyprus</a> that uses <a href="/wiki/Turkish_lira" title="Turkish lira">Turkish lira</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Including outermost regions of (<a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="R\xc3\xa9union">R\xc3\xa9union</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Collectivity_of_Saint_Martin" title="Collectivity of Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a>)</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Only the European part of the country is part of the European Union and uses the euro. The <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Netherlands" title="Caribbean Netherlands">Caribbean Netherlands</a> introduced the <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">United States dollar</a> in 2011. <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Cura\xc3\xa7ao">Cura\xc3\xa7ao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a> have their own currencies, which are pegged to the dollar.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See <a href="/wiki/Montenegro_and_the_euro" title="Montenegro and the euro">Montenegro and the euro</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Belarusian ruble is pegged to the euro, Russian ruble and US$ in a currency basket.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-46">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the quotation, the <a href="/wiki/Epsilon" title="Epsilon">epsilon</a> is actually represented with the <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyrillic">Cyrillic</a> capital letter Ukrainian ye (<a href="/wiki/%D0%84" class="mw-redirect" title="\xd0\x84">\xd0\x84</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">U+</a>0404) instead of the technically more appropriate Greek lunate epsilon symbol (<b>\xcf\xb5</b>, U+03F5).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">by means of Council Regulation 2866/98 (EC) of 31 December 1998.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-52">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">by Council Regulation 1478/2000 (EC) of 19 June 2000</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-79">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The total sum is 200% because each currency trade always involves a <a href="/wiki/Currency_pair" title="Currency pair">currency pair</a>; one currency is sold (e.g. US$) and another bought (\xe2\x82\xac). Therefore each trade is counted twice, once under the sold currency ($) and once under the bought currency (\xe2\x82\xac).  The percentages above are the percent of trades involving that currency regardless of whether it is bought or sold, e.g. the U.S. Dollar is bought or sold in 88% of all trades, whereas the Euro is bought or sold 32% of the time.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
